Limit exposure to electronic devices: The blue light emitted by screens can interfere with your sleep. Try to avoid using electronic devices, such as smartphones or laptops, for at least an hour before bed.\n\n5. Avoid stimulants: Limit your intake of caffeine, especially in the afternoon and evening, as it can disrupt your sleep. Also, be cautious with alcohol and nicotine, as they can negatively impact sleep quality.\n\n6. Exercise regularly: Engaging in regular physical activity can help improve your overall energy levels and promote better sleep. However, avoid exercising too close to bedtime, as it may make it harder to fall asleep.\n\n7. Manage stress: High levels of stress can contribute to both fatigue and insomnia. Find healthy ways to manage stress, such as practicing relaxation techniques, engaging in hobbies, or seeking support from friends, family, or a therapist.\n\n8. Evaluate your diet: Ensure you're eating a balanced diet that includes a variety of fruits, vegetables, whole grains, and lean proteins. Avoid heavy meals close to bedtime, as they can disrupt sleep.\n\nRemember, these suggestions may not work for everyone, and it's important to consult a healthcare professional for personalized advice.
